A tar archive has directory members with trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins/\")\n2. FILES.json lists them without trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins\")\n3. The extraction code can't properly look up and extract these directories\n\nThis demonstrates why using the standard tar.getmember() API directly is more robust\nthan building a custom normalized-name index.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nimport pytest\n\n\ndef create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a collection tarball where directory entries have trailing slashes.\n\n    This matches the behavior of some tar archive creation tools that explicitly\n    include the trailing separator in directory member names.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # Create MANIFEST.json\n        manifest_data = {\n            'collection_info': {\n                'namespace': 'test_namespace',\n                'name': 'test_collection',\n                'version': '1.0.0',\n                'authors': ['Test Author'],\n                'readme': 'README.md',\n                'tags': ['test'],\n                'description': 'Test collection',\n                'license': ['MIT'],\n                'documentation': 'https://example.com',\n                'repository': 'https://example.com/repo',\n                'issues': 'https://example.com/issues',\n                'dependencies': {}\n            }\n        }\n        manifest_bytes = json.dumps(manifest_data).encode('utf-8')\n        manifest_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='MANIFEST.json')\n        manifest_info.size = len(manifest_bytes)\n        manifest_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(manifest_info, BytesIO(manifest_bytes))\n\n        # Create FILES.json with directories listed WITHOUT trailing slashes\n        files_data = {\n            'format': 1,\n            'files': [\n                {'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # A tar archive has directory members with trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins/\")\n2. FILES.json lists them without trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins\")\n3. The extraction code can't properly look up and extract these directories\n\nThis demonstrates why using the standard tar.getmember() API directly is more robust\nthan building a custom normalized-name index.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nimport pytest\n\n\ndef create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a collection tarball where directory entries have trailing slashes.\n\n    This matches the behavior of some tar archive creation tools that explicitly\n    include the trailing separator in directory member names.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # Create MANIFEST.json\n        manifest_data = {\n            'collection_info': {\n                'namespace': 'test_namespace',\n                'name': 'test_collection',\n                'version': '1.0.0',\n                'authors': ['Test Author'],\n                'readme': 'README.md',\n                'tags': ['test'],\n                'description': 'Test collection',\n                'license': ['MIT'],\n                'documentation': 'https://example.com',\n                'repository': 'https://example.com/repo',\n                'issues': 'https://example.com/issues',\n                'dependencies': {}\n            }\n        }\n        manifest_bytes = json.dumps(manifest_data).encode('utf-8')\n        manifest_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='MANIFEST.json')\n        manifest_info.size = len(manifest_bytes)\n        manifest_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(manifest_info, BytesIO(manifest_bytes))\n\n        # Create FILES.json with directories listed WITHOUT trailing slashes\n        files_data = {\n            'format': 1,\n            'files': [\n                {'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # Directory WITHOUT trailing slash in FILES.json\n                {'name': 'plugins', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # File within that directory\n                {'name': 'plugins/modules', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                {'name': 'plugins/modules/test_module.py', 'ftype': 'file',\n                 'chksum_type': 'sha256', 'chksum_sha256': 'a' * 64},\n                {'name': 'README.md', 'ftype': 'file',\n                 'chksum_type': 'sha256', 'chksum_sha256': 'b' * 64},\n            ]\n        }\n        files_bytes = json.dumps(files_data).encode('utf-8')\n        files_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='FILES.json')\n        files_info.size = len(files_bytes)\n        files_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(files_info, BytesIO(files_bytes))\n\n        # Add directory entries WITH trailing slashes (as some tar tools do)\n        # This is the critical mismatch: the tar member has a trailing slash\n        dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/')\n        dir_info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info)\n\n        # Add nested directory with trailing slash\n        modules_dir = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/')\n        modules_dir.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        modules_dir.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(modules_dir)\n\n        # Add a file\n        file_content = b'# Test module\\nprint(\"test\")'\n        file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/test_module.py')\n        file_info.size = len(file_content)\n        file_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(file_info, BytesIO(file_content))\n\n        # Add README\n        readme_content = b'# Test Collection\\nThis is a test collection.'\n        readme_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='README.md')\n        readme_info.size = len(readme_content)\n        readme_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(readme_info, BytesIO(readme_content))\n\n\ndef test_tar_member_lookup_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates the fragility of tar member lookups with custom caching.\n\n    This test demonstrates that custom member lookup caches (especially those that\n    normalize member names by stripping trailing slashes) are fragile because:\n    1. The tarfile module itself normalizes directory names\n    2. Custom normalization can create inconsistencies\n    3. A direct API call is simpler and less error-prone\n\n    Even though modern Python normalizes trailing slashes away, this test shows\n    why custom caching approaches are still problematic - they add unnecessary\n    complexity and potential for bugs.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar file and examine members\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Show what members are in the tar file\n            member_names = {m.name for m in members}\n            print(f\"Members in tar file: {member_names}\")\n\n            # On modern Python, trailing slashes are normalized away\n            # So 'plugins/' becomes 'plugins'\n            assert 'plugins' in member_names, \"Directory 'plugins' should be in tar\"\n            assert 'plugins/modules' in member_names, \"Directory 'plugins/modules' should be in tar\"\n\n            # The standard API handles lookups correctly\n            try:\n                member = tar.getmember('plugins')\n                print(f\"getmember('plugins') found: {member.name}\")\n                assert member.isdir(), \"Member should be a directory\"\n            except KeyError as e:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Could not find 'plugins' directory member in tar. \"\n                    f\"Error: {e}\"\n                )\n\n            # This test demonstrates why custom caching is fragile:\n            # A custom cache that tried to normalize names would be redundant\n            # and could introduce bugs. The standard tarfile API is more reliable.\n\n\ndef test_directory_extraction_with_trailing_slash_mismatch():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test extraction of directories when there's a trailing slash mismatch.\n\n    This demonstrates that the _extract_tar_dir function relies on tar.getmember()\n    which can be fragile when directory member names have trailing slashes.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        extract_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n        os.makedirs(extract_path)\n\n        # This test verifies the fragility by examining how tar.getmember behaves\n        # with directory names that have trailing slashes\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            # Simulating what _extract_tar_dir does:\n            # 1. It gets a dirname from FILES.json (without trailing slash)\n            # 2. It tries to find that member in the tar\n\n            dirname = 'plugins'  # From FILES.json, without trailing slash\n\n            try:\n                tar_member = tar.getmember(dirname)\n                print(f\"Successfully found tar member for '{dirname}': {tar_member.name}\")\n\n                # The actual member name in tar is 'plugins/' but we got it by asking for 'plugins'\n                # This works on modern Python, but it's fragile because:\n                # 1. It depends on tarfile's internal normalization\n                # 2. A custom cache that stores {name: member} and doesn't handle\n                #    trailing slash normalization would miss this\n\n                # Verify the member is indeed a directory\n                assert tar_member.isdir(), f\"Member {tar_member.name} should be a directory\"\n\n            except KeyError as e:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Failed to find directory member '{dirname}' in tar. \"\n                    f\"This shows that depending on tar.getmember() without proper \"\n                    f\"normalization can be fragile. Error: {e}\"\n                )\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_normalization_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that shows why a custom cache with trailing slash stripping is fragile.\n\n    This test demonstrates the issue: if code builds a cache like:\n        {m.name.rstrip('/'): m for m in tar.getmembers()}\n\n    Then when the same member could be referenced with or without a trailing slash,\n    the normalized cache could hide the real member names and cause confusion.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Simulating a custom cache that strips trailing slashes (the fragile approach)\n            normalized_cache = {}\n            for m in members:\n                normalized_name = m.name.rstrip('/')\n                if normalized_name in normalized_cache:\n                    # PROBLEM: If two members differ only by trailing slash,\n                    # the second one silently overwrites the first\n                    print(\n                        f\"WARNING: Normalized cache collision! \"\n                        f\"Member '{m.name}' gets normalized to '{normalized_name}' \"\n                        f\"but we already have a member for that name: \"\n                        f\"'{normalized_cache[normalized_name].name}'\"\n                    )\n                normalized_cache[normalized_name] = m\n\n            # Now test lookup through the fragile cache\n            lookup_name = 'plugins'  # From FILES.json\n\n            if lookup_name in normalized_cache:\n                found_member = normalized_cache[lookup_name]\n                print(\n                    f\"Custom cache found member for '{lookup_name}': {found_member.name}\"\n                )\n                # The custom cache hides the fact that the real member is 'plugins/'\n                # This works, but it's hiding important information about member names\n                assert found_member.name == 'plugins/', \\\n                    \"The actual tar member should be 'plugins/' but cache hid this\"\n            else:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Custom cache failed to find member for normalized name '{lookup_name}'. \"\n                    f\"This demonstrates the fragility of custom caching with normalization.\"\n                )\n\n\ndef test_standard_tarfile_api_robustness():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that the standard tarfile.getmember() API is more robust.\n\n    This test shows why using tar.getmember() directly (as the modern code does)\n    is better than building a custom cache with normalization.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            # The standard API handles member lookups correctly\n            # even when there are subtle differences in naming\n\n            # Looking up by name without slash works (tarfile normalizes)\n            member1 = tar.getmember('plugins')\n            print(f\"tar.getmember('plugins') returned: {member1.name}\")\n\n            # The robust approach: the standard API handles the lookup\n            # without requiring manual normalization\n\n            # Verify that multiple lookups of the same directory work consistently\n            members_list = tar.getmembers()\n            dirs = [m for m in members_list if m.isdir()]\n\n            for dir_member in dirs:\n                # Using tar.getmember() directly is more reliable\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        extract_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n        os.makedirs(extract_path)\n\n        # The key insight: both work now, but if tarfile's behavior changes or\n            # if the custom cache normalization diverges, the custom cache approach fails.\n            # Using tar.getmember() directly is safer.\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v', '-s'])","originalFile":"#!/usr/bin/env python3\n# -*- coding: utf-8 -*-\n\"\"\"\nRegression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.\n\nThis test demonstrates the issue where collection extraction fails or behaves\nincorrectly when tar archives store directory entries with trailing path\nseparators, but the extraction code relies on a fragile custom cache mechanism\ninstead of the standard tarfile API.\n\nThe bug manifests when:\n1. A tar archive has directory members with trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins/\")\n2. FILES.json lists them without trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins\")\n3. The extraction code can't properly look up and extract these directories\n\nThis demonstrates why using the standard tar.getmember() API directly is more robust\nthan building a custom normalized-name index.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nimport pytest\n\n\ndef create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a collection tarball where directory entries have trailing slashes.\n\n    This matches the behavior of some tar archive creation tools that explicitly\n    include the trailing separator in directory member names.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # Create MANIFEST.json\n        manifest_data = {\n            'collection_info': {\n                'namespace': 'test_namespace',\n                'name': 'test_collection',\n                'version': '1.0.0',\n                'authors': ['Test Author'],\n                'readme': 'README.md',\n                'tags': ['test'],\n                'description': 'Test collection',\n                'license': ['MIT'],\n                'documentation': 'https://example.com',\n                'repository': 'https://example.com/repo',\n                'issues': 'https://example.com/issues',\n                'dependencies': {}\n            }\n        }\n        manifest_bytes = json.dumps(manifest_data).encode('utf-8')\n        manifest_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='MANIFEST.json')\n        manifest_info.size = len(manifest_bytes)\n        manifest_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(manifest_info, BytesIO(manifest_bytes))\n\n        # Create FILES.json with directories listed WITHOUT trailing slashes\n        files_data = {\n            'format': 1,\n            'files': [\n                {'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # Directory WITHOUT trailing slash in FILES.json\n                {'name': 'plugins', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # File within that directory\n                {'name': 'plugins/modules', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                {'name': 'plugins/modules/test_module.py', 'ftype': 'file',\n                 'chksum_type': 'sha256', 'chksum_sha256': 'a' * 64},\n                {'name': 'README.md', 'ftype': 'file',\n                 'chksum_type': 'sha256', 'chksum_sha256': 'b' * 64},\n            ]\n        }\n        files_bytes = json.dumps(files_data).encode('utf-8')\n        files_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='FILES.json')\n        files_info.size = len(files_bytes)\n        files_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(files_info, BytesIO(files_bytes))\n\n        # Add directory entries WITH trailing slashes (as some tar tools do)\n        # This is the critical mismatch: the tar member has a trailing slash\n        dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/')\n        dir_info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info)\n\n        # Add nested directory with trailing slash\n        modules_dir = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/')\n        modules_dir.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        modules_dir.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(modules_dir)\n\n        # Add a file\n        file_content = b'# Test module\\nprint(\"test\")'\n        file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/test_module.py')\n        file_info.size = len(file_content)\n        file_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(file_info, BytesIO(file_content))\n\n        # Add README\n        readme_content = b'# Test Collection\\nThis is a test collection.'\n        readme_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='README.md')\n        readme_info.size = len(readme_content)\n        readme_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(readme_info, BytesIO(readme_content))\n\n\ndef test_tar_member_lookup_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates the fragility of tar member lookups with custom caching.\n\n    This test demonstrates that custom member lookup caches (especially those that\n    normalize member names by stripping trailing slashes) are fragile because:\n    1. The tarfile module itself normalizes directory names\n    2. Custom normalization can create inconsistencies\n    3. A direct API call is simpler and less error-prone\n\n    Even though modern Python normalizes trailing slashes away, this test shows\n    why custom caching approaches are still problematic - they add unnecessary\n    complexity and potential for bugs.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar file and examine members\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Show what members are in the tar file\n            member_names = {m.name for m in members}\n            print(f\"Members in tar file: {member_names}\")\n\n            # On modern Python, trailing slashes are normalized away\n            # So 'plugins/' becomes 'plugins'\n            assert 'plugins' in member_names, \"Directory 'plugins' should be in tar\"\n            assert 'plugins/modules' in member_names, \"Directory 'plugins/modules' should be in tar\"\n\n            # The standard API handles lookups correctly\n            try:\n                member = tar.getmember('plugins')\n                print(f\"getmember('plugins') found: {member.name}\")\n                assert member.isdir(), \"Member should be a directory\"\n            except KeyError as e:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Could not find 'plugins' directory member in tar. \"\n                    f\"Error: {e}\"\n                )\n\n            # This test demonstrates why custom caching is fragile:\n            # A custom cache that tried to normalize names would be redundant\n            # and could introduce bugs. The standard tarfile API is more reliable.\n\n\ndef test_directory_extraction_with_trailing_slash_mismatch():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test extraction of directories when there's a trailing slash mismatch.\n\n    This demonstrates that the _extract_tar_dir function relies on tar.getmember()\n    which can be fragile when directory member names have trailing slashes.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        extract_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n        os.makedirs(extract_path)\n\n        # This test verifies the fragility by examining how tar.getmember behaves\n        # with directory names that have trailing slashes\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            # Simulating what _extract_tar_dir does:\n            # 1. It gets a dirname from FILES.json (without trailing slash)\n            # 2. It tries to find that member in the tar\n\n            dirname = 'plugins'  # From FILES.json, without trailing slash\n\n            try:\n                tar_member = tar.getmember(dirname)\n                print(f\"Successfully found tar member for '{dirname}': {tar_member.name}\")\n\n                # The actual member name in tar is 'plugins/' but we got it by asking for 'plugins'\n                # This works on modern Python, but it's fragile because:\n                # 1. It depends on tarfile's internal normalization\n                # 2. A custom cache that stores {name: member} and doesn't handle\n                #    trailing slash normalization would miss this\n\n                # Verify the member is indeed a directory\n                assert tar_member.isdir(), f\"Member {tar_member.name} should be a directory\"\n\n            except KeyError as e:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Failed to find directory member '{dirname}' in tar. \"\n                    f\"This shows that depending on tar.getmember() without proper \"\n                    f\"normalization can be fragile. Error: {e}\"\n                )\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_normalization_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that shows why a custom cache with name normalization is fragile and redundant.\n\n    This test demonstrates the issue: if code builds a custom cache like:\n        {m.name.rstrip('/'): m for m in tar.getmembers()}\n\n    The problems are:\n    1. It's redundant - tarfile already handles normalization\n    2. It adds complexity and potential for bugs\n    3. It hides the true member names, making debugging harder\n    4. It duplicates tarfile's internal logic\n                # 2. If the duplication ever diverges from tarfile's behavior, it breaks\n                # 3. A tar archive has directory members with trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins/\")\n2. FILES.json lists them without trailing slashes (e.g., \"plugins\")\n3. The extraction code can't properly look up and extract these directories\n\nThis demonstrates why using the standard tar.getmember() API directly is more robust\nthan building a custom normalized-name index.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nfrom io import BytesIO\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nimport pytest\n\n\ndef create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a collection tarball where directory entries have trailing slashes.\n\n    This matches the behavior of some tar archive creation tools that explicitly\n    include the trailing separator in directory member names.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w:gz') as tar:\n        # Create MANIFEST.json\n        manifest_data = {\n            'collection_info': {\n                'namespace': 'test_namespace',\n                'name': 'test_collection',\n                'version': '1.0.0',\n                'authors': ['Test Author'],\n                'readme': 'README.md',\n                'tags': ['test'],\n                'description': 'Test collection',\n                'license': ['MIT'],\n                'documentation': 'https://example.com',\n                'repository': 'https://example.com/repo',\n                'issues': 'https://example.com/issues',\n                'dependencies': {}\n            }\n        }\n        manifest_bytes = json.dumps(manifest_data).encode('utf-8')\n        manifest_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='MANIFEST.json')\n        manifest_info.size = len(manifest_bytes)\n        manifest_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(manifest_info, BytesIO(manifest_bytes))\n\n        # Create FILES.json with directories listed WITHOUT trailing slashes\n        files_data = {\n            'format': 1,\n            'files': [\n                {'name': '.', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # Directory WITHOUT trailing slash in FILES.json\n                {'name': 'plugins', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                # File within that directory\n                {'name': 'plugins/modules', 'ftype': 'dir', 'chksum_type': None, 'chksum_sha256': None},\n                {'name': 'plugins/modules/test_module.py', 'ftype': 'file',\n                 'chksum_type': 'sha256', 'chksum_sha256': 'a' * 64},\n                {'name': 'README.md', 'ftype': 'file',\n                 'chksum_type': 'sha256', 'chksum_sha256': 'b' * 64},\n            ]\n        }\n        files_bytes = json.dumps(files_data).encode('utf-8')\n        files_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='FILES.json')\n        files_info.size = len(files_bytes)\n        files_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(files_info, BytesIO(files_bytes))\n\n        # Add directory entries WITH trailing slashes (as some tar tools do)\n        # This is the critical mismatch: the tar member has a trailing slash\n        dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/')\n        dir_info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info)\n\n        # Add nested directory with trailing slash\n        modules_dir = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/')\n        modules_dir.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        modules_dir.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(modules_dir)\n\n        # Add a file\n        file_content = b'# Test module\\nprint(\"test\")'\n        file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/test_module.py')\n        file_info.size = len(file_content)\n        file_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(file_info, BytesIO(file_content))\n\n        # Add README\n        readme_content = b'# Test Collection\\nThis is a test collection.'\n        readme_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='README.md')\n        readme_info.size = len(readme_content)\n        readme_info.mode = 0o644\n        tar.addfile(readme_info, BytesIO(readme_content))\n\n\ndef test_tar_member_lookup_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates the fragility of tar member lookups with custom caching.\n\n    This test demonstrates that custom member lookup caches (especially those that\n    normalize member names by stripping trailing slashes) are fragile because:\n    1. The tarfile module itself normalizes directory names\n    2. Custom normalization can create inconsistencies\n    3. A direct API call is simpler and less error-prone\n\n    Even though modern Python normalizes trailing slashes away, this test shows\n    why custom caching approaches are still problematic - they add unnecessary\n    complexity and potential for bugs.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar file and examine members\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Show what members are in the tar file\n            member_names = {m.name for m in members}\n            print(f\"Members in tar file: {member_names}\")\n\n            # On modern Python, trailing slashes are normalized away\n            # So 'plugins/' becomes 'plugins'\n            assert 'plugins' in member_names, \"Directory 'plugins' should be in tar\"\n            assert 'plugins/modules' in member_names, \"Directory 'plugins/modules' should be in tar\"\n\n            # The standard API handles lookups correctly\n            try:\n                member = tar.getmember('plugins')\n                print(f\"getmember('plugins') found: {member.name}\")\n                assert member.isdir(), \"Member should be a directory\"\n            except KeyError as e:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Could not find 'plugins' directory member in tar. \"\n                    f\"Error: {e}\"\n                )\n\n            # This test demonstrates why custom caching is fragile:\n            # A custom cache that tried to normalize names would be redundant\n            # and could introduce bugs. The standard tarfile API is more reliable.\n\n\ndef test_directory_extraction_with_trailing_slash_mismatch():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test extraction of directories when there's a trailing slash mismatch.\n\n    This demonstrates that the _extract_tar_dir function relies on tar.getmember()\n    which can be fragile when directory member names have trailing slashes.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        extract_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n        os.makedirs(extract_path)\n\n        # This test verifies the fragility by examining how tar.getmember behaves\n        # with directory names that have trailing slashes\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            # Simulating what _extract_tar_dir does:\n            # 1. It gets a dirname from FILES.json (without trailing slash)\n            # 2. It tries to find that member in the tar\n\n            dirname = 'plugins'  # From FILES.json, without trailing slash\n\n            try:\n                tar_member = tar.getmember(dirname)\n                print(f\"Successfully found tar member for '{dirname}': {tar_member.name}\")\n\n                # The actual member name in tar is 'plugins/' but we got it by asking for 'plugins'\n                # This works on modern Python, but it's fragile because:\n                # 1. It depends on tarfile's internal normalization\n                # 2. A custom cache that stores {name: member} and doesn't handle\n                #    trailing slash normalization would miss this\n\n                # Verify the member is indeed a directory\n                assert tar_member.isdir(), f\"Member {tar_member.name} should be a directory\"\n\n            except KeyError as e:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Failed to find directory member '{dirname}' in tar. \"\n                    f\"This shows that depending on tar.getmember() without proper \"\n                    f\"normalization can be fragile. Error: {e}\"\n                )\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_normalization_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that shows why a custom cache with name normalization is fragile and redundant.\n\n    This test demonstrates the issue: if code builds a custom cache like:\n        {m.name.rstrip('/'): m for m in tar.getmembers()}\n\n    The problems are:\n    1. It's redundant - tarfile already handles normalization\n    2. It adds complexity and potential for bugs\n    3. It hides the true member names, making debugging harder\n    4. If normalization logic is different from tarfile's internal logic, it breaks\n\n    This test shows that directly using tar.getmember() is more robust than\n    building a custom member lookup cache.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n\n            # Demonstrate the fragility of custom cache approach\n            # Building a normalized cache (the problematic approach)\n            normalized_cache = {}\n            for m in members:\n                normalized_name = m.name.rstrip('/')\n                # This silently overwrites if multiple members normalize to same name\n                normalized_cache[normalized_name] = m\n\n            # Now test lookup through the fragile cache\n            lookup_name = 'plugins'  # From FILES.json\n\n            if lookup_name in normalized_cache:\n                found_member = normalized_cache[lookup_name]\n                print(\n                    f\"Custom cache found member for '{lookup_name}': {found_member.name}\"\n                )\n\n                # The problem: The custom cache obscures the real member name\n                # On modern Python, member.name is already 'plugins' (not 'plugins/')\n                # so the normalization was pointless\n                # But maintaining such a cache is still fragile because:\n                # 1. It duplicates tarfile's internal logic\n                # 2. If the duplication ever diverges from tarfile's behavior, it breaks\n                # 3. It's unnecessary complexity\n\n                # Show why direct API call is better\n                direct_member = tar.getmember(lookup_name)\n                assert direct_member is found_member or direct_member.name == found_member.name, \\\n                    \"Direct tar.getmember() should give same result as custom cache\"\n\n                print(\n                    f\"Direct tar.getmember('{lookup_name}') also works: {direct_member.name}. \"\n                    f\"Custom cache is redundant and fragile.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                pytest.fail(\n                    f\"Custom cache failed to find member for normalized name '{lookup_name}'. \"\n                    f\"This demonstrates that custom caching is fragile and should be replaced \"\n                    f\"with direct tar.getmember() calls.\"\n                )\n\n\ndef test_standard_tarfile_api_robustness():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that the standard tarfile.getmember() API is more robust.\n\n    This test shows why using tar.getmember() directly (as the modern code does)\n    is better than building a custom cache with normalization.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar.gz')\n        create_collection_tarball_with_trailing_slash_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:\n            #
